A context is returned which is canceled on one of these signals. If a second signal is caught, the program is terminated with exit code 1.\n\n## Location\n\nThe function is located in `sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/manager/signals` package. An older implementation in `pkg/runtime/signals` is deprecated in favor of `pkg/manager/signals`.\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nThe function creates a context with cancellation, sets up a signal notification channel with capacity for 2 signals, and spawns a goroutine that cancels the context on the first signal and calls os.Exit(1) on the second signal.\n\n## Common Usage Pattern\n\nThe typical usage is with a manager, where `mgr.Start(signals.SetupSignalHandler())` passes the signal handler context to the manager's Start method.\n\n## Two-Stage Shutdown Pattern\n\nThis implements a graceful shutdown pattern where the first signal triggers graceful shutdown via context cancellation, and a second signal forces immediate termination to handle cases where the process doesn't shut down gracefully.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e9ff51c6-9d17-44b8-9f91-c832ba26ce71","uuid":"955e3cdb-e4f6-404c-a4e1-5603b48b636e","tool_use_result":{"query":"kubernetes controller-runtime signals SetupSignalHandler","results":[{"tool_use_id":"srvtoolu_015FESWmCyBdkDRdVNJpjgsq","content":[{"title":"signals package - Exit directly.\n    }()\n    \n    return ctx\n}\n```\n\n## Key Features\n\n**Signal Registration:** \"signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\" registers handlers for termination signals (SIGTERM/SIGINT).\n\n**Double-Signal Protection:** The goroutine waits for a second signal and immediately exits with code 1, preventing graceful shutdown delays.\n\n**Single-Call Enforcement:** The `close(onlyOneSignalHandler)` panics if called twice, ensuring only one signal handler is registered.\n\n**Graceful Shutdown:** The context cancellation on first signal allows the application to perform cleanup operations."}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e9ff51c6-9d17-44b8-9f91-c832ba26ce71","uuid":"3e5cc14a-178f-4636-8216-a83ed14e1fbb","tool_use_result":{"bytes":196590,"code":200,"codeText":"OK","result":"# Signal Handling Functions in Kubernetes APIServer\n\nBased on the source code, here are the key signal handling functions:\n\n## SetupSignalHandler()\nThis function returns a channel that closes when SIGTERM or SIGINT is received:\n```go\nfunc SetupSignalHandler() <-chan struct{} {\n    return SetupSignalContext().Done()\n}\n```\n\n## SetupSignalContext()\nThis is the core implementation that manages signal registration:\n```go\nfunc SetupSignalContext() context.Context {\n    close(onlyOneSignalHandler) // panics when called twice\n    \n    shutdownHandler = make(chan os.Signal, 2)\n    \n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n    go func() {\n        <-shutdownHandler\n        cancel()\n        <-shutdownHandler\n        os.Exit(1) // second signal. Analysis\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus implements comprehensive graceful shutdown in `cmd/prometheus/main.go` through a termination handler that coordinates multiple shutdown pathways. The signal handler registration uses Go's standard `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)` to capture both SIGINT and SIGTERM signals on a buffered channel (approximately lines 1450-1475).\\n\\nThe shutdown mechanism leverages the `oklog/run.Group` library to manage graceful termination of interconnected components. The critical cleanup ordering enforces a sequence that prevents data corruption: (1) Web handler stops first to prevent new requests, (2) Scrape manager halts to stop writing to storage, (3) Storage/TSDB closes to flush pending writes, (4) Rule manager stops. This ordering ensures storage isn't closed while scrapers actively write data. The implementation includes multiple shutdown triggers: OS signals (SIGTERM/SIGINT), web service requests, and internal cancellation signals, with proper coordination through channel closure and context cancellation.\\n\\nReferences:\\n- [prometheus/cmd/prometheus/main.go - main branch](https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/blob/main/cmd/prometheus/main.go)\\n- [Anatomy of Graceful Shutdown: Part 5](https://mrlokans.work/posts/anatomy-of-graceful-shutdown-part-5/)\\n\\n### Kubernetes (kubernetes/apiserver and kubernetes/kubernetes)\\n\\nKubernetes implements signal handling at two levels:\\n\\n**1. Core Signal Handler (kubernetes/apiserver repository):**\\nThe `pkg/server/signal.go` file in the kubernetes/apiserver repository contains the fundamental signal handling logic with two key functions:\\n\\n- `SetupSignalHandler()`: Returns a channel that closes when SIGTERM or SIGINT is received\\n- `SetupSignalContext()`: The core implementation that creates a context and registers signal handlers using `signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)` for SIGTERM and SIGINT on a buffered channel with capacity 2\\n\\nThe implementation features a two-signal protection pattern: the first signal triggers graceful shutdown by canceling the context, allowing the application to perform cleanup; if a second signal is received, the program immediately calls `os.Exit(1)` to force termination. This prevents indefinite hanging during shutdown. The single-call enforcement via `close(onlyOneSignalHandler)` ensures only one signal handler is registered.\\n\\n**2. Server Integration (kubernetes/kubernetes):**\\nBoth the kube-apiserver (`cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`) and kubelet (`cmd/kubelet/app/server.go`) call `genericapiserver.SetupSignalContext()` to create a shutdown context. The kube-apiserver uses `server.Shutdown()` to gracefully terminate HTTP connections without dropping bytes. The kubelet uses the context in its main `run()` function, monitoring `<-ctx.Done()` to initiate graceful termination. Cleanup ordering in the kubelet includes: health checker startup, Kubernetes API client initialization, container manager setup, event recorder establishment, kubelet startup, systemd readiness notification, and finally waiting for context cancellation.\\n\\nReferences:\\n- [kubernetes/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go - master branch](https://github.com/kubernetes/apiserver/blob/master/pkg/server/signal.go)\\n- [kubernetes/cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go - master branch](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/master/cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go)\\n- [kubernetes/cmd/kubelet/app/server.go - master branch](https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/master/cmd/kubelet/app/server.go)\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana uses a delegated signal handling architecture where signal registration occurs in parent initialization functions rather than the main entry point. The `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go` file is minimal (11 lines), containing only `os.Exit(cmd.RunGrafanaCmd(\\\"server\\\"))` which delegates to the cmd utility package.\\n\\nThe graceful shutdown is implemented through two key files:\\n\\n**1. Server Shutdown (`pkg/server/server.go`):**\\nThe `Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string)` method handles termination using a `sync.Once` to ensure single execution. It delegates to `managerAdapter.Shutdown()` to terminate background services, logs the shutdown reason, and implements context-based timeout protection. Callers can specify timeout duration when invoking `Shutdown()`.\\n\\n**2. HTTP Server Implementation (`pkg/api/http_server.go`):**\\nThe `Run()` method implements graceful shutdown through context cancellation. A goroutine monitors the context and, when cancelled (triggered by external signal handlers), calls `httpSrv.Shutdown(context.Background())` to gracefully close active connections. The actual signal handler registration for SIGTERM/SIGINT occurs in a parent initialization function that creates and passes the context to `Run()`, following a pattern that separates signal handling concerns from HTTP server concerns.\\n\\nReferences:\\n- [grafana/pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go - main branch](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/blob/main/pkg/cmd/grafana-server/main.go)\\n- [grafana/pkg/server/server.go - main branch](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/blob/main/pkg/server/server.go)\\n- [grafana/pkg/api/http_server.go - main branch](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/blob/main/pkg/api/http_server.go)\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nAll three projects implement graceful SIGTERM/SIGINT shutdown but with different architectural patterns:\\n- **Prometheus** uses explicit signal.Notify() with oklog/run.Group for coordinated component shutdown\\n- **Kubernetes** uses a centralized SetupSignalContext() pattern with two-signal protection in its apiserver package\\n- **Grafana** uses context-based delegation where signal handlers are registered in parent functions, allowing flexible shutdown coordination\\n\\nCommon patterns across all three include: (1) signal.Notify() for SIGTERM/SIGINT registration, (2) context cancellation for propagating shutdown signals, (3) graceful HTTP server shutdown without dropping connections, and (4) ordered cleanup of dependent components to prevent data corruption during termination.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2328,"cache_read_input_tokens":56369,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2328},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e9ff51c6-9d17-44b8-9f91-c832ba26ce71","uuid":"a40dbd00-0eac-45f9-9a74-224868548570"}
